Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|1|1.7
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|2|<blockquote>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|2|<p class="content"><b>Automatic</b></p>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|3|<p class="content">The Automatic probe attempts to determine whether the device speaks SNMP or whether simply to ping the device.</p>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|4|<p class="content">InterMapper sends a SNMP GetNextRequest for the sysName, sysObjectID, and sysServices OIDs (1.3.6.1.2.1.1.5.5, 1.3.6.1.2.1.1.5.2, and 1.3.6.1.2.1.1.5.7, respectively) using the specified SNMP Read-only community string. If a proper SNMP response is received, InterMapper sets the device's probe to be SNMP; otherwise, InterMapper sets the device to use a Ping/Echo probe.</p>

Servers-Proprietary/Big Brother Probe|com.dartware.bigbrother|3|<p class="content">This probe allows you to use InterMapper as a Big Brother "BBDISPLAY" to collect information sent by Big Brother clients.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Big Brother Probe|com.dartware.bigbrother|4|<p class="content"><i>Purple Time</i> is the number of minutes to wait without a report before indicating a problem. In an actual Big Brother server, this is thirty minutes; Big Brother will show a device as purple if it goes this long without reports from the device. We will show it as DOWN (blinking red).</p>

Servers-Proprietary/BlitzWatch|com.dartware.blitzwatch|1|1.5
Servers-Proprietary/BlitzWatch|com.dartware.blitzwatch|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Proprietary/BlitzWatch|com.dartware.blitzwatch|2|<p class="content"><b>BlitzWatch</b></p>
Servers-Proprietary/BlitzWatch|com.dartware.blitzwatch|3|<p class="content">The protocol used to monitor the performance of a <u>BlitzMail</u> server. BlitzMail is a TCP/IP-based client-server electronic mail system developed at Dartmouth College. In the BlitzMail system, all mail and mail preferences are stored on one or more BlitzMail servers, thus giving a user access to their email from anywhere. The BlitzWatch probe provides a simple view into the current state of a single BlitzMail server in terms of simultaneous user count, CPU utilization, and disk transfer statistics.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/BlitzWatch|com.dartware.blitzwatch|4|</blockquote><p class="content">

Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|1|1.3
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>SQL Query</b> </p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe establishes an ADO connection to Microsoft SQL Server running on the target host.  It issues the query you specify and displays the returned fields.  If no records are returned the status of the device is set to Critical.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|4|<p class="content">The Query parameter is the SQL query you wish to perform.  It should be enclosed in double-quotes.  Using the "TOP" keyword in your query will likely make it return faster.  You may wish to specify specific columns in your query and include a "WHERE" or an "ORDER BY" clause.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|5|<p class="content">The Rows and Columns parameters allow you to limit the output of your query to the first "Columns" fields of the first "Rows" records returned.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|6|<p class="content">The Instance parameter specifies the SQL Server instance you wish to query on the target host.  If you wish to query the default instace you should leave this blank.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|7|<p class="content">The Database parameter specifies the database on the target instance to be queried.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|8|<p class="content">The User parameter may be a SQL Server user on the target host, or may take the form of "domain\\user" for a domain login.  Leave it blank if integrated authentication is desired.  The user must have been granted dbreader privilege to the database.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|9|<p class="content">The Timeout (sec) parameter allows you to override the timeout set on the device.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|10|<p class="content">InterMapper invokes the sql_query.vbs VB script which must reside in the Tools sub-directory of the InterMapper Settings directory.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|11|</blockquote><p class="content">

It generates random data for the traffic on all its links, so that there is something to look at. These traffic data are chartable, as well, and can be used for demonstrating strip charts.</p>
Miscellaneous/Demo Probe|com.dartware.demo|4|<p class="content">The device also toggles between the UP/OK and Down state when manually reprobed. Consequently, it's also easy to show what happens when a device goes down, especially for manual dependencies.</p>
Miscellaneous/Demo Probe|com.dartware.demo|5|<p class="content">For simple maps, the parameters below can be set to zero. To create complicated, heavily-interconnected demonstration maps, try setting the parameters to 10 and 50, respectively. </p>
Miscellaneous/Demo Probe|com.dartware.demo|6|<p class="content"><i>Link Count</i> is the number of interfaces to create when first adding the device to the map. </p>
Miscellaneous/Demo Probe|com.dartware.demo|7|<p class="content"><i>Loop %</i> is the percentage of links that should connect themselves to subnets that are already present on the map. </p>

Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|1|2.0
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|2|<p class="content"><b>DHCPv4</b></p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|3|<p class="content">The protocol used by IP clients to obtain an IPv4 address and other parameters for using TCP/IP. Depending on your setup, this probe may only work if your computer is already using an IP address acquired using BOOTP or DHCP.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|4|<p class="content">Note: On Mac OS X, this probe will only work if there are no enabled DHCP, Bootp, or PPP interfaces.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|5|<p class="content">This probe sends DHCP-INFORM requests to test the DHCP mechanism for an IP subnet.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|6|<p class="content"><i>BOOTP Relay Address</i> is the IP address to which all DHCP requests are addressed. Normal BOOTP/DHCP requests are broadcast to the local subnet (255.255.255.255), where they are picked up by the BOOTP agent in a router and relayed to the BOOTP/DHCP server. If this parameter is empty, InterMapper sends the DHCP requests directly to the target IP address specified for the device.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|7|<p class="content"><i>DHCP Client ID</i> is an optional parameter included with InterMapper's request that can be used to identify the DHCP client as InterMapper. If you leave this parameter blank, InterMapper does not include the DHCP Client ID option in its DHCP probe.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|8|<p class="content"><i>DHCP Subnet Mask</i> is an optional parameter specifying the expected value of the subnet mask returned by the DHCP server. If you leave this parameter blank, InterMapper will accept any subnet mask value.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|9|<p class="content"><i>DHCP Router Address</i> is an optional parameter specifying the expected value of the router address returned by the DHCP server. If you leave this parameter blank, InterMapper will accept any router address value.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|10|<p class="content"><i>DHCP Message Type</i> is the type of DHCP message to send. Typically, you should prefer DHCP-INFORM, since this message type will not cause an IP address to be allocated by the DHCP server. A DHCP server may respond to a DHCP-DISCOVER request by wastefully leasing out an IP address which will never be used.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|11|<p class="content"><i>Hardware Address</i> is an optional parameter specifying the MAC address of the network interface that should be used to send the DHCP request.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|12|<p class="content"><i>Request Seconds</i> is an optional parameter specifying the number of seconds to claim we have been trying for; certain DHCP servers (such as the one supplied with OS X 10.5 with the default settings) will not respond at all until the client claims to have been trying for at least 10 seconds.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|13|</blockquote><p class="content">
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|14|<i>Filename: com.dartware.dhcp</i><br />
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|15|<i>Version: 2.0</i><br />
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|16|</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|1|1.8
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|2|<p class="content"><b>Domain Name Service (DNS): (A) Address</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|3|<p class="content">The protocol used by TCP/IP network clients to translate Internet names into IP addresses, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1034.txt">RFC 1034</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1035.txt">RFC 1035</a>. This probe sends a DNS request to look up the IP address for a specified domain name.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|4|<p class="content"><i>Domain Name</i> is the fully qualified domain name you are attempting to resolve.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|5|<p class="content"><i>IP Address</i> allows you to optionally specify an IP address the domain name should resolve to. If this parameter is non-empty, InterMapper will report a status from the specified <i>Failure Status</i> parameter if one of the returned IP addresses doesn't match the one given here.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|6|<p class="content"><i>Recursion Desired</i> tells the target DNS server whether it can ask another DNS server for help in answering the request. If the target DNS server does not know how to resolve the given domain name, and "Recursion-Desired" is true, the target DNS server may query an authoritative DNS server. To prevent other servers from becoming involved, set "Recursion Desired" to false.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|7|<p class="content"><i>Failure Status</i> is the device status InterMapper should report when the IP address in a DNS response doesn't match the specified <i>IP Address</i> parameter. You can choose to have InterMapper set the device status to Down, Alarm or Warning. The default is to report IP address mismatches as an Alarm condition, so that Down is reserved for when the DNS server fails to respond at all.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|8|</blockquote><p class="content">
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|9|<i>Filename: com.dartware.dns</i><br />
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|10|<i>Version: 1.8</i><br />
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|11|</p>

Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|3|<p class="content">The protocol used by TCP/IP network clients to translate Internet names into Text records, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1034.txt">RFC 1034</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1035.txt">RFC 1035</a>. This probe sends a DNS request to look up the text record for a specified domain name.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|4|<p class="content"><i>Domain Name</i> is the fully qualified domain name you are attempting to resolve.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|5|<p class="content"><i>Text Substring</i> allows you to optionally specify a substring of a text record the domain name should resolve to. Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|1|1.8
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|2|<p class="content"><b>Remote Authentication Dial-in User Service (RADIUS)</b></p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|3|<p class="content">The protocol used by remote access servers to authenticate dial-in users, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2138.txt">RFC 2138</a>. This probe tests a RADIUS server by sending an Access-Request packet to authenticate a specific user name and password. Before you can use this probe with a particular RADIUS server, you must add the InterMapper computer's IP address to the RADIUS server and choose a "shared secret" for it. The "shared secret" is used by the RADIUS protocol to encrypt passwords in RADIUS requests. A RADIUS server will not answer access-requests from a client it doesn't recognize.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|4|<p class="content">The officially assigned port number for RADIUS is 1812. However, some RADIUS servers use port number 1645 for historical reasons.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|5|<p class="content"><i>Shared Secret</i> is InterMapper's unique password into the RADIUS server. The same value needs to be configured into the RADIUS server as well, as it is used for authentication.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|6|<p class="content"><i>User Name</i> is the user you are trying to authenticate.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|7|<p class="content"><i>Password</i> is the user's password. This password is encrypted using the shared secret; it is not sent in the clear.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|8|</blockquote><p class="content">

Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe extracts jitter test data from a Cisco IP SLA agent that is running on a Cisco router or switch. Typically these jitter tests are used to measure jitter, latency, and packet loss for VoIP and video conferencing applications.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|4|<p class="content"><i>SNMP Index</i> is the value used on the "ip sla monitor" command when configuring the IP SLA agent in the Cisco switch or router (see example below). This value identifies the jitter test, and is the SNMP index used by Intermapper to probe the device. To probe for different instances of jitter tests on a single Cisco switch or router, create separate devices on your Intermapper map each with a different SNMP Index. </p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|5|<p class="content"><i>Latency Alarm Threshold</i> is the ALARM threshold for latency in milliseconds. If Average Latency value exceeds this threshold the device will enter the Alarm state.</p>

Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|8|<p class="content"><i>Jitter Warning Threshold</i> is the WARNING threshold for Jitter. If the Average Jitter value exceeds this threshold the device will go into the Warning state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|9|<p class="content"><i>Packet Loss Alarm Threshold</i> is the ALARM threshold for Packet Loss. If the Percent Packet Loss value exceeds this threshold, the device will enter the Alarm state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|10|<p class="content"><i>Example</i></p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|11|<p class="content">Example IOS commands for configuring an IP SLA jitter test to run on a Cisco router or switch:</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|12|<p class="content">ip sla monitor 250</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|13|<p class="content">  type jitter dest-ipaddr w.w.w.w dest-port 50505 source-ipaddr x.x.x.x num-packets 2000 interval 20</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|14|<p class="content">  request-data-size 256 </p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|15|<p class="content">  owner yyyy</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|16|<p class="content">  tag zzzz</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|17|<p class="content">  exit</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|18|<p class="content">In the above example "250" is the SNMP index to use. This can be any value as long as it is unique. "w.w.w.w" is the IP address of the remote IP SLA responder. "x.x.x.x" is the local IP address of this IP SLA agent. "yyyy" is any text information identifying the owner of the test (e.g., name of network service provider). "zzzz" is any text information identifying this particular test.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|19|<p class="content">To schedule the IP SLA test to run forever: </p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|20|<p class="content">ip sla monitor schedule 66 life forever start-time now</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|21|<p class="content">To start the IP SLA responder on the remote IP SLA responder:</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|22|<p class="content">ip sla monitor responder</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|23|<p class="content">In the above IOS commands the jitter test does not specify a codec type, and so ICPIF and MOS scores are not available. If the test is modified to include a codec type then minor revisions will be required to this SNMP probe. Also, some routers and switches may not support the MIB variables for ICPIF and MOS scores - this depends on the IOS train. </p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|24|<p class="content">More information about configuring Cisco IP SLA is available on the www.cisco.com site.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|25|</blockquote><p class="content">
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|26|<i>Filename: com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt</i><br />

SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|1|1.8
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|2|<blockquote>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>SNMP Table Viewer Probe </b></p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe displays the contents of several useful tables from common SNMP MIBs. It retrieves its data by walking the SNMP data values in the tables.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|4|<p class="content"><b>ifTable</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|5|<p class="content">The "Interfaces" table gives information about the physical and logical interfaces of the device. It displays the following columns: <i>ifIndex</i>, <i>ifDescr</i>, <i>ifType</i>, <i>ifSpeed</i>, <i>ifPhysAddress</i>, <i>ifOperStatus</i>, and <i>ifAdminStatus</i>. It is defined in MIB-II (RFC-1213) and updated in the IF-MIB.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|6|<p class="content"><b>ifXTable</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|7|<p class="content">The Extended Interfaces table defined in IF-MIB. This is an extended version of ifTable and adds the <i>ifName</i> and <i>ifAlias</i> fields/columns to those shown in the ifTable above.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|8|<p class="content"><b>Traffic Counters</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|9|<p class="content">This table displays the traffic counters: ifInOctets and ifOutOctets from the MIB-II ifTable, and the ifHCInOctets and ifHCOutOctets from the IF-MIB. To determine the traffic rate, refresh the window and compare two separate readings. The difference divided by the time between the refreshes (in seconds) will be the number of bytes/second.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|10|<p class="content"><b>tcpConnTable</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|11|<p class="content">Displays information about any connections that are present: Variables include <i>tcpConnLocalAddress</i>, <i>tcpConnLocalPort</i>, <i>tcpConnRemAddress</i>, and <i>tcpConnRemPort</i>. It is defined in MIB-II.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|12|<p class="content"><b>udpTable</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|13|<p class="content">Displays information about any UDP listeners that are present: Variables include <i>udpLocalAddress</i>, <i>udpLocalPort</i>. It is defined in MIB-II.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|14|<p class="content"><b>ipAddrTable</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|15|<p class="content">This table displays the IP address/mask/broadcast address for each interface. Includes <i>ipAdEntAddr</i>, <i>ipAdEntifIndex</i>, <i>ipAdEntNetMask</i>, <i>ipAdEntBcastAddr</i>,  and <i>ipAdEntReasmMaxSize</i>. It is defined in RFC-1213, and updated in the IP-MIB. </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|16|<p class="content"><b>ipRouteTable</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|17|<p class="content">This table (currently deprecated) comes from RFC-1213 (MIB-II). </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|18|<p class="content"><b>ipCidrRouteTable</b> and <b>ipForwardTable</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|19|<p class="content">These tables come from the IP-FORWARD-MIB, which displays information about CIDR multipath IP Routes. Note: the ipForwardTable obsoletes the ipRouteTable of MIB-II, and is in turn obsoleted by the ipCidrRouteTable.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|20|<p class="content"><b>ipNetToMediaTable</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|21|<p class="content">The Net Address to Media Address table (also known as the "ARP Table") displays these fields/columns: <i>ipNetToMediaIfIndex</i>, <i>ipNetToMediaNetAddress</i>, <i>ipNetToMediaPhysAddress</i>, and <i>ipNetToMediaType</i>. It is defined in RFC-1213.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|22|<p class="content"><b>dot1dTpFdbTable</b> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|23|<p class="content">The "Bridge MIB" (RFC1493) displays the forwarding database for transparent bridges. </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|24|<p class="content">The Status Window contains links to each of these tables. Click the link to see the contents of the table on the selected device.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|25|<p class="content">This probe requires that you first import these MIBs: <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1213.txt">RFC1213-MIB (MIB-II)</a>, <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1493.txt">Bridge MIB (rfc1493)</a>, <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2011.txt">IP-MIB (rfc2011)</a>, <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2863.txt">IF-MIB (rfc2863)</a>, and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2096.txt">IP-FORWARD-MIB (rfc2096).</a> These are all bundled together in a <a href="http://intermapper.com/support/users/probes.html#tableviewer">single zip archive.</a> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|26|</blockquote><p class="content">
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|27|<i>Filename: com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt</i><br />
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|28|<i>Version: 1.8</i><br />
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|29|</p>

Miscellaneous/TCP Check|com.dartware.snmp.tcpcheck|3|<p class="content">This probe generates an alarm if the count of TCP connections is greater than the "Allowed TCP Connections" parameter. This probe can be used to detect people telnetting into a box that shouldn't have connections (perhaps, a router that might be attacked from outside your network).</p>
Miscellaneous/TCP Check|com.dartware.snmp.tcpcheck|4|<p class="content">This SNMP probe retrieves the device's 'tcpCurrEstab' MIB variable and compares its value to the maximum number of TCP connections allowed. If the number of established TCP connections exceeds the limit, this probe will put the device into "Alarm" status.</p>
Miscellaneous/TCP Check|com.dartware.snmp.tcpcheck|5|<p class="content"><i>Allowed TCP Connections</i> is the threshold for the number of TCP connections allowed. If the number of connections exceeds this value, the device will alarm.</p>

SNMP/SNMP - High Util|com.dartware.snmp.traffic-util.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe monitors the <i>utilization</i> of ifInOctets and ifOutOctets traffic statistics of a particular interface on the device, and sets the device into alarm or warning when the traffic exceeds certain utilization thresholds. </p>
SNMP/SNMP - High Util|com.dartware.snmp.traffic-util.txt|4|<p class="content">It also gives a DOWN alarm if the interface's ifOperStatus is not equal to 1 (up).</p>

SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|2|<blockquote>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>Trap Viewer Probe</b></p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe listens for trap packets to arrive and displays the contents of the trap in the Status Window. It does not actively poll the device, nor does it take any action based on the trap contents. </p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|4|<p class="content">You can view all the variables that have been parsed from the trap packet in the device's Status Window. You can also use this as a prototype for making your own trap probes.</p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|5|<p class="content"><b>How the Trap Viewer Probe Works</b></p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|6|<p class="content">When a trap arrives, the probe parses the trap to get the values from the trap's header as well as the first ten items in its Varbind List. It assigns all these values to variables that can be used in the probe and displayed in the Status Window.</p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|7|<p class="content">To see how this probe works, you can configure your equipment to send traps to InterMapper, or use the net-snmp <b>snmptrap</b> command. Either way, the Status Window will show the values present in any traps that arrive.</p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|8|<p class="content">For more information on the <b>snmptrap</b> command, read the net-snmp documentation for the <a href="http://www.net-snmp.org/tutorial/tutorial-4/commands/snmptrap.html">trap tutorial</a> and the <a href="http://www.net-snmp.org/docs/man/snmpinform.html">snmptrap command</a>. The remainder of this note shows how to send a trap with variables from the Dartware MIB:</p>

Miscellaneous/Legacy/SNMP v2c|com.dartware.snmpv2c|2|<p class="content"><b>SNMP v2c</b></p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/SNMP v2c|com.dartware.snmpv2c|3|<p class="content">This is a legacy probe, provided for compatibility with InterMapper Traditional and older versions of InterMapper (< 4.4). If you are using InterMapper server, please use the SNMP MIB-II probe instead and set the probe's SNMP version to SNMP v2 in the Probe Info window.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/SNMP v2c|com.dartware.snmpv2c|4|<p class="content">The SNMP v2c probe retrieves MIB-II information from the device. This includes sysLocation, sysContact, and sysUptime from the system group, and traffic (bytes/second, packets/second, errors/minute) for each of the interfaces.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/SNMP v2c|com.dartware.snmpv2c|5|<p class="content">It also uses the 64-bit counters for interface traffic stats to provide accurate information (without rollover) on very high speed links.</p>

Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|1|1.10
Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|2|<blockquote>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|2|<p class="content"><b>SNMP - Cisco (v2c)</b></p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|3|<p class="content">This is a legacy probe, provided for compatibility with InterMapper Traditional and older versions of InterMapper (< 4.4). If you are using InterMapper server, please use the Cisco - Process and Memory Pool probe instead and set the probe's SNMP version to SNMP v2 in the Probe Info window.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|4|<p class="content">This probe monitors the CPU and Memory utilization of a Cisco router using SNMPv2c.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|5|<p class="content"><i>CPU Busy - Alarm</i> is the ALARM threshold for CPU utilization. If the average percentage of CPU usage over a 1 minute interval exceeds this threshold, the device will enter the Alarm state.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|6|<p class="content"><i>CPU Busy - Warning</i> is the WARNING threshold for CPU utilization. If the average percentage CPU usage over a 1 minute interval exceeds this threshold, the device will enter the Warning state.</p>

Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|1|2.6
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>Barracuda Spam Firewall (HTTP)</b></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|3|<p class="content">This TCP probe queries a <a href="http://www.barracudanetworks.com/">Barracuda Spam Firewall</a> for various performance statistics.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|4|<p class="content">The BASIC->Status page of the Administrators interface is retrieved via HTTP.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|5|<p class="content"><i>User</i> is the name of the administrator.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|6|<p class="content"><i>Password</i> is the password for administrator.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|7|<p class="content"><i>Port</i> is the Barracuda's Web Interface HTTP Port set on the BASIC->Administration page.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|8|<p class="content"><b>Thresholds</b></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|9|<p class="content"><i>In/Out Queue Size</i>: X In/ X Out - both values should be less than 100.  If either value consistently exceeds 100 for greater than 30 minutes that MAY mean there is a problem that needs to be looked at.  Sometimes the value will rise temporarily and then go back down after 10 or 15 minutes.  </p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|10|<p class="content">This is normal behavior for the Inbound Queue and can be the result of an orchestrated attack.  The Barracuda will attempt to read in as many messages as it can and that will tend to slow down the processing rate, which in turn means an increase in the queue size.  If the Outbound Queue increases that usually means that the destination server is unavailable or the local DNS is not working.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|11|<p class="content">Recommendation - If either queue exceeds 100 for more than 15 minutes = WARNING, if either queue exceeds 500 for more than 30 minutes = ALARM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|12|<p class="content"><i>Average Latency</i>: X seconds - Is the average time it takes to receive, process and deliver the last 30 messages.  It should normally be below 50 seconds.  If it is consistently over 50 seconds for greater than 30 minutes that MAY mean there is a problem that needs to be looked at.  Sometimes the value will rise temporarily and then go back down after 10 or 15 minutes.    This is normal behavior.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|13|<p class="content">Recommendation - If average latency exceeds 50 seconds for more than 15 minutes = WARNING, if average latency exceeds 150 seconds for more than 30 minutes = ALARM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|14|<p class="content"><i>Last Message</i>: X minute ago - For a busy machine this value should be low, normally less than 5 minutes.  If it is consistently over 20 minutes for greater than 30 minutes that MAY mean there is a problem</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|15|<p class="content">that needs to be looked at.  Sometimes the value will rise temporarily and then go back down after 2 or 3 minutes.  This is normal behavior.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|16|<p class="content">Recommendation - If last message exceeds 15 minutes = WARNING, if last message exceeds 30 minutes = ALARM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|17|<p class="content"><i>Unique Recipients</i>: X number - This number represents the number of unique email addresses processed over the past 24 hours.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|18|<p class="content">Recommendation - No general rule possible.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|19|<p class="content"><i>CPU 1 Fan Speed</i>: X RPM - Should be between 3,000 and 5,000 RPM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|20|<p class="content"><i>CPU 2 Fan Speed</i>: X RPM - Should be between 3,000 and 5,000 RPM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|21|<p class="content">Recommendation - If either CPU fan speed is less than 2500 = WARNING, if either fan speed is less than 500 = ALARM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|22|<p class="content"><i>Redundancy (RAID)</i>:  Fully Operational - If this ever says that they are NOT fully operational that is a problem that needs to be looked at.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|23|<p class="content">Recommendation - If RAID says it is no fully operational for more than 2 hours = WARNING, if RAID says it is not fully operational for more than 48 hours = ALARM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|24|<p class="content"><i>Firmware Storage</i>: X % - Should be somewhere between 60 - 80%.  If it exceeds 80% that usually means that a debug file needs to be deleted.  This can be done on a non-emergency basis.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|25|<p class="content">Recommendation - If firmware storage exceeds 80% = WARNING, if firmware storage exceeds 90% = ALARM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|26|<p class="content"><i>Mail/Log Storage</i>: X % - Should be somewhere between 1 - 70%.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|27|<p class="content">Recommendation - If mail/log storage exceeds 70% = WARNING, if mail/log storage exceeds 80% = ALARM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|28|<p class="content"><i>System Load</i>: X % - Can vary wildly between 1 and 100% during normal operation.  If it stays at 100% for greater than 2 hours that MAY mean there is a problem that needs to be looked at.   Sometimes the value will rise temporarily and then go back down after 2 or 3 minutes. This is normal behavior.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|29|<p class="content">Recommendation - If System Load is higher than 80% for more than 1 hour = WARNING, if System Load is higher than 95% for more than 3 hours = ALARM</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|30|<p class="content"><i>CPU Temperature</i>: Should be between 40 and 70 degrees C</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|31|<p class="content">Recommendation - If CPU Temp is higher than 70 degrees C for more than 30 minutes = WARNING, if CPU TEMP is higher than 80 degrees C for more than 1 hour = ALARM		</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|32|</blockquote><p class="content">

Servers-Standard/Basic TCP|com.dartware.tcp.basic|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP|com.dartware.tcp.basic|2|<p class="content"><b>Basic TCP Connection Test</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP|com.dartware.tcp.basic|3|<p class="content">This basic TCP probe tests whether a TCP port accepts connections or not. If the specified port accepts the TCP connection, the device is reported UP. If the specified port fails to accept the TCP connection within sixty seconds, the device is reported DOWN.</p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP|com.dartware.tcp.basic|4|</blockquote><p class="content">
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP|com.dartware.tcp.basic|5|<i>Filename: com.dartware.tcp.basic</i><br />

Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|1|1.5
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|2|<p class="content"><b>Basic TCP (Blocked)</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|3|<p class="content">This basic TCP probe tests that a TCP port is <b>not</b> accepting connections. This probe may be used to test that a firewall is working properly, or that a particular TCP service is never operating on an important machine.</p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|4|<p class="content">If the specified port accepts the TCP connection, the device is reported with the desired failure status. If the specified port fails to accept the TCP connection within 120 seconds, the device status is "OK".</p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|5|<p class="content"><i>Failure Status</i> is the device status that InterMapper should report when a TCP connection is made. The default is DOWN.</p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|6|</blockquote><p class="content">

Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|2|<p class="content"><b>Custom TCP Probe</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|3|<p class="content">This probe lets you send your own string over the TCP connection and set the status of the device depending on the response received. There are six parameters which control the operation of this probe:</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|4|<p class="content"><i>String to send</i> is the initial string sent over the TCP connection. This could be a command which indicates what to test, or a combination of a command and a password. The string is sent on its own line, terminated by a CR-LF.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|5|<p class="content"><i>Seconds to wait</i> is the number of seconds to wait for a response.  If no response is received within the specified number of seconds, the device's status is set to DOWN.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|6|<p class="content"><i>OK Response</i> is the substring which should match the device's "ok response". If it matches the first line received, the device is reported to have a status of OK.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|7|<p class="content"><i>WARN Response</i> is the substring which should match the device's warning response.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|8|<p class="content"><i>ALRM Response</i> is the substring which should match the device's alarm response.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|9|<p class="content"><i>CRIT Response</i> is the substring which should match the device's critical response.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|10|<p class="content"><i>DOWN Response</i> is the substring which should match the device's down response.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|11|<p class="content">If InterMapper cannot connect to the specified TCP port, the device's status is set to DOWN.</p>

Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|9|<p class="content"><i>User Agent</i> is the string that identifies this InterMapper client probe to the proxy web server. Some proxy servers block traffic at the proxy based on the User-Agent identity. This parameter lets you optionally override InterMapper's default User-Agent setting. If you leave this parameter blank, InterMapper sends a User-Agent  string of "InterMapper/version", where version is the current version number of InterMapper.</p>

Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|1|0.8
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|2|<blockquote>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>InterMapper Engine Status</b></p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe monitors the status of the InterMapper polling engine. With the default setting, this probe displays the results of 500 loops through the polling engine. To measure activity at a finer-grain, decrease the value of the loops parameter. Setting the "loops" parameter to the value 1 will update the statistics on every pass through the main run loop.</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|4|<p class="content">The "Main Loop" frequency is the number of times that InterMapper performs the main loop each second. The theoretical maximum loop frequency is 66.667 loops per second, based on the current yield value of 15 msec. If it falls below 10 or even 5 loops per second, InterMapper may report false outages.</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|5|<p class="content">This probe also reports polling rate as a percentage of the maximum loops per second. This is a measure of how much additional processing occurs per loop. This percentage will never be 100%. It should, however, level out and remain steady over time.</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|6|<p class="content">On Unix systems, this probe reports Context Switches Per Loop (CSPL). This is another measure of the overhead of InterMapper's processing as it runs on your system. Fewer context switches per loop is better (ideal = 0), since context switches carry overhead. A server with thousands of devices and hundreds of mays may well have a CSPL greater than 2 during normal operation. (This value is not available on Windows systems, and is alway set to -1.)</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|7|<p class="content">InterMapper tracks the number of bytes sent out the main UDP polling socket. Bytes/Loop is the average bytes sent per loop, averaged over the last batch of N loops. Bytes Peak is the maximum number of bytes sent in a *single* polling loop. Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|1|1.2
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|2|<blockquote>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>Nagios NRPE over SSL/TLS</b></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|3|<p class="content">The NRPE ("Nagios Remote Plugin Executor") protocol defines a way to execute Nagios plugins on remote machines. After you install a Nagios NRPE daemon and and one or more Nagios plugins on a remote machine, InterMapper uses the following procedure to retrieve the status of that machine.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|4|<p class="content"><li class="content"> Establish an encrypted SSL/TLS connection to the remote NRPE daemon</li></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|5|<p class="content"><li class="content"> Request that a specific Nagios plugin be executed</li></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|6|<p class="content"><li class="content"> Receive the response from the plugin</li></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|7|<p class="content"><li class="content"> Parse the response and display the state of that machine.</li></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|8|<p class="content">The NRPE daemon uses a configuration file (<i>nrpe.cfg</i>) that has command definition entries in this form:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|9|<p class="content"><code>  command[check_swap]=/usr/local/nagios/libexec/check_swap -w 20% -c 10%</code></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|10|<p class="content">When the NRPE daemon receives a request to run the "check_swap" plugin, it issues the command above.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|11|<p class="content">The <i>Nagios Plugin</i> paramenter tells which plugin to execute. It must match one of the command definitions in the nrpe.cfg file, e.g., the text within square brackets [ ... ]. To test the connection from InterMapper to the NRPE daemon, set <i>Nagios Plugin</i> to the value "_NRPE_CHECK".</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|12|<p class="content">For information about installing an NRPE daemon, see the <a href="http://nagios.sourceforge.net/docs/nrpe/NRPE.pdf">NRPE Documentation</a> (at http://nagios.sourceforge.net/docs/nrpe/NRPE.pdf), especially the section on Remote Host Configuration. Nagios and the Nagios logo are registered trademarks of Ethan Galstad. For more information, see <a href="http://www.nagios.org.">http://www.nagios.org.</a> </p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|13|</blockquote><p class="content">

If you specify a multicast IP address, InterMapper will listen for packets directed to that multicast address.  This probe will change the device status to the DOWN if a packet isn't received within specified number of seconds (the default is 10 seconds).</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|4|<p class="content">The Multicast Listener probe can be used to verify that a multicast source is broadcasting, for example, a live QuickTime broadcaster.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|5|<p class="content">This probe does not inject any traffic into the network; it is passive only.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|6|<p class="content"><i>Multicast IP Address</i> is the optional multicast IP address to listen on.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|7|<p class="content"><i>Seconds to wait</i> is the maximum number of seconds to wait between packets.  If a packet is not received within the specified number of seconds, the device's status is set to DOWN. The "Seconds to wait" timer is reset every time a packet is received.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|8|<p class="content"><i>Verify Source Address</i> lets you specify whether the probe should only count packets from the IP address of the targeted device.</p>

WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|1|1.10
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|2|<blockquote>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>WMI CPU Utilization</b> </p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe uses WMI to retrieve the percentage of time that a processor is executing a non-idle thread on the target host.  Specifically, it queries the PercentProcessorTime property of the Win32_PerfFormattedData_PerfOS_Processor class and compares it against the Warning and Critical parameters you set.  Each processor is compared against the Single Warning and Critical parameters, and the total CPU utilization is compared with the Total Warning and Critical criteria.  Any of these values can be left blank if that check is not desired.</p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|4|<p class="content">The target host must be running Windows XP, Windows Server 2003 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|5|<p class="content">The User parameter be a local user on the target host, or may take the form of "domain\\user" for a domain login.  Leave it blank if authentication is not required, such as when the target is the localhost.</p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|6|<p class="content">InterMapper invokes the cpu_util.vbs companion script which was placed in the Tools folder of the InterMapper Settings folder when this probe was loaded.  It uses the exit value to set the condition of the device and the performance data returned by the script to create a nice display of chartable data.</p>

Zero-sized drives (i.e. an empty cd-rom) will not be listed.  The first drive failing the warning or critical criteria will be the one cited in the reason.</p>

WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|7|<p class="content">The Hours, Minutes and Seconds parameters combine to define how far back in the event log to search.  These parameters are subtracted from the current time and used to select events based on when they were written to the log.</p>

WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe uses WMI to retrieve information about files on the target host.  Specifically, it queries the CIM_DataFile class, limiting the search with the parameters you set.  The target host must be running Windows 2000 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|4|<p class="content">The Path parameter specifies the location of the files you wish to check.  It should include the drive and be enclosed in double-quotes if it contains spaces.  </p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|5|<p class="content">The File parameter contains the filename and extension of the file you wish to check.  The path will be prepended to it during the final query.  If it is blank, all files in the folder specified by the Path that meet the Size or time criteria will be listed.  File may also be set to a list of comma-separated filenames which will each be prepended by the Path and used as query criteria.  </p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|6|<p class="content">Wildcards (* ?) may be used in the filename.  If wildcards are used, be sure to specify the Path parameter or the query might take an inordinate amount of time.  At least one of the File or Path parameters must be set.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|7|<p class="content">The Size parameter defines the minimum filesize criteria in bytes.  Any files larger than this value will be listed.  The Hours, Minutes and Seconds parameters combine to define how recently the file had to be changed to be listed.  These parameters are subtracted from the current time and used to select files based on their LastModified value.  At least one of these parametrs must be set.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|8|<p class="content">The User parameter may be a local user on the target host, or may take the form of "domain\\user" for a domain login.  Leave it blank if authentication is not required, such as when the target is the localhost.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|9|<p class="content">InterMapper invokes the file_chk.vbs companion script which was placed in the Tools folder of the InterMapper Settings folder when this probe was loaded.  It lists the files which meet your criteria and uses the exit value to set the condition of the device.</p>

WMI/WMI System Information|com.dartware.wmi.system_infomation.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>WMI System Information</b> </p>
WMI/WMI System Information|com.dartware.wmi.system_infomation.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe uses WMI to collect a variety of information about the monitored host including hardware and operating system details.  The target host must be running Windows 2000 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI System Information|com.dartware.wmi.system_infomation.txt|4|<p class="content">The User parameter may be a local user on the target host, or may take the form of "domain\\user" for a domain login.  Leave it blank if authentication is not required, such as when the target is the localhost.</p>
WMI/WMI System Information|com.dartware.wmi.system_infomation.txt|5|<p class="content">InterMapper invokes the system_info.vbs companion script which was placed in the Tools folder of the InterMapper Settings folder when this probe was loaded.</p>

WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|1|1.10
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|2|<blockquote>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>WMI Top Processes</b> </p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe uses WMI to retrieve information about CPU utilization and processes running on the target host.  Specifically, it queries the PercentProcessorTime property of the Win32_PerfFormattedData_PerfOS_Processor class and compares it against the Warning and Critical parameters you set.  It queries the PercentProcessorTime property of the Win32_PerfFormattedData_PerfProc_Process class and lists up to five processes using the most CPU time.  Because there is a time lapse between collecting the CPU data and the process data, the reported values will not add up exactly.  The target host must be running Windows XP, Windows Server 2003 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|4|<p class="content">The User parameter may be a local user on the target host, or may take the form of "domain\\user" for a domain login.  Leave it blank if authentication is not required, such as when the target is the localhost.</p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|5|<p class="content">InterMapper invokes the top_cpu.vbs companion script which was placed in the Tools folder of the InterMapper Settings folder when this probe was loaded.  It uses the exit value to set the condition of the device and the performance data returned by the script to create a nice display of chartable data.</p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|6|</blockquote><p class="content">
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|7|<i>Filename: com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt</i><br />

Wireless/Alvarion/Alvarion B-14 & B-28 (BU)|com.dartware.wrls.alvarion.b14.master.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe monitors an <a href="http://www.alvarion.com">Alvarion</a> B-14 or B-28 base unit (BU). It retrieves and displays the radio band, operating frequency, and slave association. It will go into an alarm when no slave is associated, and when the operating frequency doesn't match the configured frequency. Traffic information is available for the ethernet and radio interfaces. (To show the ethernet interface, we recommend using the "Display unnumbered interfaces" behavior.)</p>
Wireless/Alvarion/Alvarion B-14 & B-28 (BU)|com.dartware.wrls.alvarion.b14.master.txt|4|<p class="content">This probe is part of the InterMapper Wireless Probe Bundle, and requires InterMapper 4.2.1 or later.</p>

Wireless/Alvarion/Alvarion B-14 & B-28 (RB)|com.dartware.wrls.alvarion.b14.slave.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>Alvarion B-14 & B-28 (Slave)</b></p>
Wireless/Alvarion/Alvarion B-14 & B-28 (RB)|com.dartware.wrls.alvarion.b14.slave.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe monitors an <a href="http://www.alvarion.com">Alvarion</a> B-14 or B-28 remote bridge (RB) unit. It retrieves and displays the radio band, operating frequency, average received signal to noise ratio, and the MAC address of the associated base unit (BU). It will go into alarm or warning states based on user-defined parameters for a low signal to noise ratio or high traffic on a specified interface.</p>

Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|2|<blockquote>
Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>Redline AN50</b></p>
Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe is meant to probe a <a href="http://www.redlinecommunications.com">Redline</a> AN50 point-to-point radio, acting as either a master or slave. It retrieves and displays a number of critical statistics for the radio, and gives alarms if it goes out of user-specified thresholds.  The probe retrieves:</p>
Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|4|<p class="content"><b>Average RF Rx signal strength</b> and compares it to the Rx Signal alarm and warning thresholds specified below.</p>
Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|5|<p class="content"><b>Average RF SNR</b> and compares it to the signal to noise ratio alarm and warning thresholds specified below.</p>
Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|6|<p class="content"><b>Signaling Burst Rate</b> The device goes into alarm when the Uncoded Burst Rate is less than the specified code. (Codes are 0=6Mb/s,1=9Mb/s,2=12Mb/s,3=18Mb/s,4=24Mb/s,5=36Mb/s,6=48Mb/s,7=54Mbs)</p>
Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|7|<p class="content"><b>Operating frequency</b> The device goes into alarm if it's different from the value specified below.</p>
Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|8|<p class="content"><b>Radio Link Status</b> The device goes into alarm if it's not connected.</p>
Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|9|<p class="content">This probe is part of the InterMapper Wireless Add-on pack, and requires InterMapper 4.2.4 or later.</p>
Wireless/Redline/AN50|com.dartware.wrls.redlinean50.txt|10|</blockquote><p class="content">

Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|1|2.9
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|2|<blockquote>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|2|<p class="content"><b>Victron UPS</b></p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|3|<p class="content">This probe monitors some needfull USV parameters.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|4|<p class="content"><i>UPS Battery Status - Alarm</i> is the ALARM threshold for Battery Status.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|5|<p class="content">\i\If the value is 2 USV working normal.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|6|<p class="content">\i\If the value is 1 USV is on bypass, the device will enter the Alarm</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|7|<p class="content">state.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|8|<p class="content"><i>UPS Battery Remaining - Warning</i> is the WARNING threshold for the</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|9|<p class="content">estimated battery time remaining. If the Battery Remaining is less than</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|10|<p class="content">this threshold, the device will enter the Warning state.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|11|<p class="content"><i>UPS Battery low Voltage - Warning</i> is the WARNING threshold for the</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|12|<p class="content">min. battery voltage. If the Battery voltage is less than this threshold,</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|13|<p class="content">the device will enter the Warning state.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|14|<p class="content"><i>Low Input Voltage line 1 - Alarm</i> is the ALARM threshold for min input</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|15|<p class="content">voltage on phase 1. If the input voltage drops below this threshold, the</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|16|<p class="content">device will enter the Alarm state.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|17|<p class="content"><i>Low Input Voltage line 2 - Alarm</i> is the ALARM threshold for min input</p>
